./ ADD NAME=$$$NOTE  0101-02141-02142-1002-00029-00001-00000-SBGOLOB

  This member is for the THORNTON member of CBT Tape File 570, a
  general collection of advice "how to do stuff".

  This file refers to Dick Thornton's way of doing stuff.  I have
  included his entire "MEMORY" file from File 564 of the CBT Tape,
  here.  This contains his miscellaneous "how to do stuff" things,
  which is what File 570 is all about.....

  Use PDSLOAD (program from CBT Tape File 093, load module on
  File 035) to create a pds from this member.

  Please refer to Files 558 thru 565 of the CBT Tape for the majority
  of the contributions from Dick Thornton.

  For Dick's other contributions:  Files 217, 234 are disassemblers
                                   Files 568, 569 are old TSO games

  emails (whatever currently applies - use these for starters):

     Dick Thornton:    dickthor@hotmail.com
                       cthornton@swva.net
                       rthornton@trigon.com

     Sam Golob:        sbgolob@attglobal.net
                       sbgolob@aol.com



./ ADD NAME=$$README 0101-02141-02141-1423-00148-00226-00000-BC0THOR
***********************************************************************
* MEMORY library: Contains general lore I needed to get the job done. *
*                As I got older and my long and short term memories   *
*                faded, I needed some way to remember how to do those *
*                things I only did once in a while, but were critical *
*                when the need arose. Then all I had to do was        *
*                remember to look in there. This will be of most value*
*                to older System Programers who haven't yet developed *
*                a system of their own. Still, I have provided a      *
*                short description of each member below.              *
***********************************************************************
ACF2      .Some common ACF2 commands.
ADDR31    .Sample assembler code for 31-bit addressing, page 1 of 2.
ADDR312   .Sample assembler code for 31-bit addressing, page 2 of 2.

./ ADD NAME=ADDR31   0114-91011-98247-1138-00057-00058-00000-BC0THOR
_______________________________________________________________________________
|     |09/04/98                                            ADDR31              |
|     |              ADDRESSING: 31-BIT                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     | XYZ     CSECT                                                          |
|     | XYZ     AMODE  xx   (24,31,ANY. Default=24)                            |
|     | XYZ     RMODE  xx   (24,ANY. Default=24)                               |
|     |        -- OR --                                                        |
|     | //LKED EXEC PGM=IEWL,PARM=(AMODE=xx,RMODE=x                            |
|     |                                                                        |
|     | AMODE specifies mode when entered via LINK,                            |
|     | ATTACH, or XCTL, not by BALR, BC, etc                                  |
|     |                                                                        |
|     | LKED RUN unit settings:                                                |
|     |   ANY CSECT AMODE=24  Y   N   -                                        |
|     |   LOAD MODULE RMODE=  -  24  ANY                                       |
|     |   ASM AMODE=         ANY ANY ANY                                       |
|     |   ASM RMODE=         ANY ANY ANY                                       |
|     |   - - - - - - - - - - - - - - - -                                      |
|     |   Set AMODE=          24 ANY  31                                       |
|     |   Set RMODE=          24  24 ANY                                       |
|     |                                                                        |
|     | BAL, BALR, BAS, BASR, CLCL, EDMK, LA, LRA,                             |
|     | MVCL, TRT are affected by AMODE                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |   BSM   R1,R2   Sets PSW AMODE bit into hi bit of R1 if                |
|     |                 R1 > 0. Sets hi bit of R2 into PSW AMODE               |
|     |                 and branches to address in R2 if R2 > 0.               |
|     |                 Same as BASSM except no NSI address to R1              |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |   BASSM R1,R2   R1 gets current PSW AMODE and NSI address              |
|     |                 if R1 > 0. If R2 > 0, its contents set in              |
|     |                 PSW AMODE and NSI address. Same as BSM                 |
|     |                 except R1 gets NSI address.                            |
|     |                                                                        |
|     | LOAD macro returns addr mode in R0 hi bit:                             |
|     | from AMODE=RMODE=24 ==> AMODE=31,RMODE=ANY                             |
|     |  LOAD  EP=A31ANY      ----->    .                                      |
|     |  ST    R0,EPADDR     |          .                                      |
|     |        .             |          .                                      |
|     |        .             |  LM  R14,R12,12(r13)                            |
|     |  L     R15,EPADDR    |  BSM 0,R14 ---                                  |
|     |  BASSM R14,R15 - - -                 |                                 |
|     |        . <---------------------------                                  |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |  Get into 31-bit mode from below 16M line:                             |
|     |             ICM   R1,15,*+6                                            |
|     |             BSM   0,R1                                                 |
|     |             DC    X'80',AL3(*+3)                                       |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |  Get back into 24-bit mode when executing below the line:              |
|     |             ICM   R1,15,*+6                                            |
|     |             BSM   0,R1                                                 |
|     |             DC    X'00',AL3(*+3)                                       |
|_____|________________________________________________________________________|
./ ADD NAME=ADDR312  0100-02015-02015-1446-00058-00058-00000-BC0THOR
_______________________________________________________________________________
|     |01/15/2002             ADDRESSING: 31-BIT (continued)           ADDR312 |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |BAL and BALR instructions are the old, pre-virtual instructions for     |
|     |    branching to the second operand address, while including the return |
|     |    address in the first operand register. The difference is that the   |
|     |    BAL and BALR instructions place the Instruction Length Code (ILC),  |
|     |    Condition Code (CC), and Program mask bits in the high order byte   |
|     |    of the R1 register followed by the 24-bit instruction address from  |
|     |    the updated PSW when executing in AMODE=24. When executing in       |
|     |    AMODE=31, BAL and BALR operate exactly like BAS and BASR: the R1    |
|     |    register gets the full rightmost 4 bytes of the updated PSW         |
|     |    including the AMODE bit.                                            |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |LA instruction when operating in AMODE=24 clears the high-order byte of |
|     |    the R1 register to zero, and loads the 24-bit address from the      |
|     |    second operand into the low-order 3 bytes. When executing in        |
|     |    AMODE=31, the R1 register high order bit is set to zero, and the    |
|     |    31-bit second operand address is placed in the low order 31 bits.   |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |BASSM instruction is used to perform routines that may be in a different|
|     |    address mode than the current program. It operates exactly like the |
|     |    BALR and BASR instructions, except that the high order bit of the   |
|     |    second operand register is used to set the PSW AMODE bit. Also, in  |
|     |    AMODE=31, the high order bit of the R1 register is set to '1' while |
|     |    the entire high-order byte of the R1 register is set to zero when   |
|     |    in AMODE=24.                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |BSM  instruction is intended to be used as the standard return from a   |
|     |    performed program whose caller may be in a different addressing     |
|     |    mode, since the full 32-bits of the R2 register replace the roght   |
|     |    hand 4 bytes of the current PSW, including the AMODE bit. For a     |
|     |    non-zero R1, the AMODE bit in the PSW is stored in the high-order   |
|     |    bit of the R1 register before the R2 register is processed.         |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |BAS and BASR are provided for calls between programs using the same     |
|     |    addressing mode.                                                    |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |BASSM and BSM are provided for calls between programs that may be in    |
|     |    different addressing modes:                                         |
|     |    Caller:              L     R15,=V(SUBPGM)  Point to external pgm    |
|     |                         BASSM R14,R15         Branch with return adr   |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |    Called return:       L     R14,12(R13)     Pick up return addr      |
|     |                         BSM   0,R14           Return to caller         |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|_____|________________________________________________________________________|

|     |01/15/2002       - - - A P F - - -                                  APF |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |CVTAUTHL (CVT+1E4) points to area containing:                           |
|     |off len  descr                                                          |
|     |+0   2   # Entries in APF list                                          |
|     |Each Entry (1st begins at +2):                                          |
|     |+0   1   Entry Length = dsname length + 6                               |
|     |+1   6   Volume Serial                                                  |
|     |+7   v   DSNAME                                                         |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |To add, change, or delete an APF entry on the fly, in TMONMVS:          |
|     |  Command: APFLIST (enter)                                              |
|     |  Cursor to 1st entry and enter (do not type anything, just enter)      |
|     |  When the APF LIST Update screen appears, type in the data set name    |
|     |    and volume serial (or SMS), then cursor to the appropriate action   |
|     |    field and type an 'S' (enter).                                      |
|     |  When asked, press (enter) to take the action, or type CAN (enter).    |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |

./ ADD NAME=AUXSTOR  0106-98247-02018-0801-00057-00057-00000-BC0THOR
_______________________________________________________________________________
|     |01/18/2002             Auxiliary Storage                         AUXSTOR|
|     |                                                                        |
|     |Aux Storage Shortage:                                                   |
|     |1) Will be reported on a particular system (A or B)                     |
|     |2) Often is temporary, caused by DUMPSRV dumping an IMS region.         |
|     |3) Procedure for curing the problem:                                    |
|     |   a) Bring up TMON on the affected system, type Q on the command line  |
|     |      cursor to Auxiliary Storage Status and note the Local Slots       |
|     |      Available %. If near 35% and DUMPSRV is near top of the list it   |
|     |      may improve soon. Watch. If it improves, do nothing.              |
|     |   b) To add a page dataset:                                            |
|     |      1) In TMON, enter Q to get to the Quick Access menu, then cursor  |
|     |         to Page Dataset Allocation and press enter. Note all local     |
|     |         datasets in the list. PAGEx2.LOCAL thru PAGEx7.LOCAL are       |
|     |         assigned at IPL.                                               |
|     |      2) In TSO on the affected system, use =3.4 (=4.1.4 in WB) with    |
|     |         a mask of SYS1.PAGEx* (x is A or B for the system). Look for   |
|     |         the first dataset with a low node of LOCAL2 that is not already|
|     |         allocated. If there are none, try LOCAL3, etc. If none are     |
|     |         available, call the DASD On-Call for space and run the job in  |
|     |         PDS.JCL(DEFPAGEx).                                             |
|     |      3) In TSO on the affected system, use the SYSCON command to get   |
|     |         a console window and enter: PA PAGE=pagedatasetname            |
|     |      4) Using TMON on the affected system, check to see the new page   |
|     |         dataset is allocated, and the shortage removed.                |
|     |                                                                        |
|     | See SYS1.PARMLIB(IEASYS00) for current IPL page datasets.              |
|     |                                                                        |
|     | Jim Price created a spare page dataset for SYSA on PRDM33 named        |
|     | SYS1.PRDM33.LOCAL which is to be used for Aux Storage Shortages only.  |
|     | Also:                                                                  |
|     | SYSA: SYS1.PAGEAK.LOCAL and SYS1.PAGEA0.LOCAL                          |
|     | SYSB: SYS1.PAGEB8.LOCAL                                                |
|     |                                                                        |
|     | MVS messages IRA400E, IRA401E, IRA403E,  and IRA500E signal Pageable   |
|     | storage problems that are not related to page datasets. Use QuickRef   |
|     | to analyze the problem/action. Basically, the available pool of memory |
|     | frames available is very low due to the number of fixed frames. The job|
|     | having the largest number of fixed frames is swapped out until the     |
|     | shortage is relieved.                                                  |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|_____|________________________________________________________________________|

|     |08/16/2000             BOOK MANAGER                             BOOKMGR |

./ ADD NAME=CICS     0105-99095-02015-1507-00057-00057-00000-BC0THOR
_______________________________________________________________________________
|     |01/15/2002             CICS                                     CICS    |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |Current release is 4.10                                                 |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |CEMT and AFCS must be entered in upper case!!!                          |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |LOGONID = PASSWORD for AFCS                                             |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |When a CICS region initializes, it issues the commands found in PLT's   |
|     |which are used to perform application initialization.                   |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |To avoid userid lockout, issue CESF LOGOFF after issuing the Netman NCCI|
|     |command to start the NCCI transaction. If only LOGOFF is issued, your   |
|     |userid is locked to the NCCI transaction and your userid will be        |
|     |"in use", preventing you from logging on after the LOGOFF is issued.    |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |CEMT I,TAS shows executing tasks                                        |
|     |CEMT I,FI(*) shows file status                                          |
|     |CEMT I,PROG(pgmname) inquires on the status of a program                |
|     |CSMT NEW,PGRMID=pgmname loads a program for use                         |
|     |CEMT SET PROG(pgmname) NEW (same as above, newer method)                |
|     |CEMT I,DA(*) lists all files in use                                     |
|     |CECI cicscmd executes a CICS command                                    |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |JCL to issue CICS commands (which protects your userid) is in members   |
|     |CICSCMND and CICSCMDS of BC0THOR.PDS.JCL.                               |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |To free a dataset held by a CICS application:                           |
|     | 1) Login to the CICS application.                                      |
|     | 2) Press the Pause key to clear the screen.                            |
|     | 3) Enter (in caps) CEMT INQ DA(ddname) and press Enter.                |
|     | 4) On the display screen overtype OPE ENA with CLO DIS and press enter.|
|     | 5) PF3 and LOGOFF when through.                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |To change a file to point to a different dataset, first free it         |
|     |as above steps 1-4, then:                                               |
|     | a) Type in the new dsname and press Enter.                             |
|     | b) Overtype CLO DIS with OPE ENA and press Enter.                      |
|     | c) The steps are all required. It won't work if you try to combine     |
|     |    steps a and b.                                                      |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |Transaction dumps CODE=ASRA: shows PSW line. Last byte of 3rd word is   |
|     |interrupt code, first two words are the PSW. Last word in the symptoms  |
|     |line is program name. In the dump, do a FIND PSW until the literal      |
|     |"REGS&PSW" is found in memory. Registers 0-15 follow the literal, then  |
|     |the PSW and ILC and CC.                                                 |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |AADF (all caps) gives ABEND-Aid FX info for an abend.                   |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |Precompiler DFHECP1$ documented in SC33-1169 "CICS/ESA Application      |
|     |  Programming Guide" in 1.1.6 Translator options. In BookManager the    |
|     |  manual id is DFHLSH23.                                                |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |

|     |01/15/2002             C Programming Language                   CLANG   |
|     |                       5647A01 V2R6M0 OS/390 C                          |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |To make ISPF edit enter and display square brackets as x'BA' and x'BB": |
|     |In Reflection, select the Setup Menu, then the Terminal option, and     |
|     |check the Country Extended Graphics Code box. In Reflection, select the |
|     |Setup Menu, Keyboard option and UN-select the Show APL Box, then select |
|     |the left-square-bracket key on the top keyboard display. Set the lower  |
|     |display to Commands and enter .TransmitANSI"[". Repeat for the right    |
|     |square bracket.                                                         |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |The above solves the data-entry and display problems with brackets, but |
|     |the value used is not that required by the C compiler, which is x'AD'   |
|     |and x'BD'. To solve this, include a step to execute program CBRAKETS    |
|     |preceding the compile step to convert brackets to compiler values in a  |
|     |temporary file sent to the compiler. See BC0THOR.PDS.JCL(EDCCB).        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |Also need terminal type=3277A. In workbench: 0 (Parameter) 1(Terminal)  |
|     |  3277A.                                                                |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |In Reflection, the upper-case 6 (hat symbol) is x'B0' and the  symbol  |
|     |is changed to the solid vertical bar.                                   |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |In C, printf() writes to the SYSPRINT DD, and perror() to SYSOUT        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |The BKT edit macro can be issued to convert brackets to the x'BA' and   |
|     |x'BB' values useful in TSO/ISPF Edit. This is useful for source         |
|     |programs uploaded from the PC, or copied from sample libraries, for     |
|     |example. It also counts and compares the number of left brackets to the |
|     |number of right brackets and reports any discrepancy.                   |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |IBM C Language datasets have high level node CBC. The CBC.SCBCSAM PDS   |
|     |contains a number of sample programs that show how to accomplish many   |
|     |programming tasks in C.                                                 |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |PROCs for use with the C Language begin with the letters ED and have    |
|     |various combinations of compile, pre-link, and linkedit. Also see       |
|     |BC0THOR.PDS.JCL(EDCCB).                                                 |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |The TSO BOOKS command makes volume 1 of the IBM manuals CD available    |
|     |online. The C Language books have identifiers beginning with CBC. Some  |
|     |useful books are in the ALL-OS390-Disc 7 bookshelf (some are on Disc 1):|
|     |1&7 CBCOLR03 SC09-2360 OS/390 V2R6.0 C/C++ Language Reference           |
|     |1&7 CBCOPG03 SC09-2362 OS/390 V2R6.0 C/C++ Programming Guide            |
|     |1&7 CBCOUG03 SC09-2361 OS/390 V2R6.0 C/C++ User's Guide                 |
|     |1&7 CBCOCR04 SC09-2361 OS/390 V2R6.0 C/C++ IBM Open Class Library       |
|     |                                     Reference                          |
|     |1&7 CBCOCU03 SC09-2363 OS/390 V2R6.0 C/C++ IBM Open Class Library       |
|     |                                     User's Guide                       |
|     | 7  CBCOMG04 SC09-2359 OS/390 V2R6   C/C++ Compiler and Run-Time        |
|     |                                     Migration Guide                    |
|     | 7  EDCLBM05 SC28-1663 OS/390 V2R6.0 C/C++ Run-Time Library Reference   |
|     |    CEEAZ010  Language Environment Programming Guide                    |
|     |    CEEA3010  Language Environment Programming Reference                |

./ ADD NAME=CLANG2   0104-00249-02015-1533-00057-00057-00000-BC0THOR
_______________________________________________________________________________
|     |09/05/2000             C Programming Language (continued)       CLANG2  |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |JCL DD statements for C programs:                                       |
|     |1) SYSPRINT is used for PRINTF output. If omitted, it is dynamically    |
|     |   allocated.                                                           |
|     |2) STDOUT01 is the default output file, STDIN01 is the default input    |
|     |   file, STDERR01 is the default error file. All are dynamically alloc- |
|     |   ated as needed.                                                      |
|     |3) If fopen() specifies a DSNAME, that dataset is allocated, if it      |
|     |   exists, otherwise it is dynamically allocated.                       |
|     |4) If fopen() specifies a DDNAME, the JCL DD statement is used, if      |
|     |   present, otherwise the DD is dynamically allocated to a temporary    |
|     |   dataset that is deleted at end of job.                               |
|     |5) sigioerr() writes to DDNAME SYSOUT. It is dynamically allocated if no|
|     |   found in the JCL.                                                    |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |When fopen() specifies a ddname for output, it is dynamically allocated |
|     |to a temporary file if the DD statement is not in the JCL (or if the    |
|     |ddname is mispelled). When a data set name is specified for output, it  |
|     |will be used, if cataloged, otherwise a new dataset will be allocated   |
|     |automatically.                                                          |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |fopen("a.b",...)   opens tsouid.A.B                                     |
|     |fopen("'BC0THOR.A.B'",...)   opens BC0THOR.A.B                          |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |Following are some mainframe datasets containing C language source,     |
|     |load modules, JCL, etc:                                                 |
|     |      CBC.TRIGON.FUNCLIST   A list of available C-language functions    |
|     |      CBC.TRIGON.SAMPJCL    JCL for the sample programs                 |
|     |      CBC.TRIGON.SAMPLOD    Load modules for the sample programs        |
|     |      CBC.TRIGON.SAMPSRC    C-language source for the sample programs   |
|     |      BC0THOR.PDS.C         C-language source for more programs         |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |The C-language compiler accepts the following (only):                   |
|     |  Backslash: x'E0'     Left square bracket: x'AD'                       |
|     |  Right Square Bracket: x'BD'    Hat (uppercase 6): x'5F'               |
|     |  Logical OR symbol (vertical bar): x'4F'. Other symbols seem to        |
|     |  be represented by values standard to IBM, Reflection, etc.            |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |

./ ADD NAME=COBOL    0108-91177-00229-0950-00057-00068-00000-BC0THOR
_______________________________________________________________________________
|     |08/16/2000              COBOL                                      COBOL|
|     |                                                                        |
|     |VS COBOL R2.3 compiler is in COB4.COBLINK: 5740-CB1                     |
|     |VS COBOL R2.4 compiler is in SYS1.VSCOLIB: 5740-CB1                     |
|     |COBOL II Runtime library is SYS1.COB2LIB: 5668-958                      |
|     |COBOL390 compiler is in IGY.V2R1M0.SIGYCOMP                             |
|     |Language Environment libraries are CEE.SCEELKED and CEE.SCEERUN         |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |COBOL II Dump Reading and Re-engineering                                |
|     | . Displays in a dump have three instructions:                          |
|     |       L    2,92(0,13)     TGTFIXD+92                                   |
|     |       L    15,44(0,2)     V(IGZCDSP)                                   |
|     |       LA   1,nnn(0,10)    PGMLIT AT +mmm                               |
|     |       BALR 14,15                                                       |
|     |   The area pointed to by register 1 begins with X'01' and ends with    |
|     |   X'FF'. Between is one or more 10-byte records, each describing a     |
|     |   field to be displayed:                                               |
|     |      +0 (1) Data type: X'00'=COMP, X'80'=COMP-1 or COMP-2, X'20'=COMP-3|
|     |                        X'40'=all other data types (displayed as-is).   |
|     |      +1 (1) Field length (when data type = X'40', this is X'00')       |
|     |      +2 (1) ?                                                          |
|     |      +3 (1) Display length (when data type = x'80', this is X'00')     |
|     |      +4 (1) Field Origin: X'08' means the field is a literal coded in  |
|     |                           the display statement and is found via R10.  |
|     |                           X'09' means the field is located via a 'cell'|
|     |                           in the TGT pointed to by R13.                |
|     |      +5 (3) Cell Offset. Usually x'000000' when origin is x'08'. For   |
|     |                          Origin X'09' this is the offset added to R13  |
|     |                          to locate the 4-byte 'cell' in the TGT.       |
|     |      +8 (2) Field Offset. The address of the field to be displayed is  |
|     |                           the sum of this offset and the TGT cell (or  |
|     |                           R10 of Origin is X'08')                      |
|     |   Example field for the display of a literal and a packed number such  |
|     |   as: DISPLAY 'TOTAL RECORDS READ = ' RECS-READ.                       |
|     |   R1 points to: X'014000001508000000012620030005090001C40043FF'        |
|     |   First field: X'4000000015080000000126' As-is data, 21 bytes long, a  |
|     |                literal in the display located in the CGT via R10+0126  |
|     |   Second field: X'20030005090001C40043' COMP-3 DATA, 3 bytes long but  |
|     |                requiring 5 bytes in the display area. First find the 4 |
|     |                byte TGT 'cell' at R13+0001C4. The field is located at  |
|     |                cell+0126.                                              |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |   After initialization, COBOL II programs maintain the TGT address in  |
|     |   R13. Often the PGT address will be in R12 and the CGT address in R10.|
|     |   The PGT address can be found in a dump at program load point +58 hex.|
|     |   The program start address (after initialization) is found at load    |
|     |   point +68 hex. The instruction at this address is a L  R10,nn(0,R12) |
|     |   where nn is the offset from the PGT to the address of the CGT.       |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |   In XPEDITER, DP programname displays storage at the first instruction|
|     |                               coded in the procedure division.         |
|     |                DP WORKING-STORAGE displays start of working storage.   |
|     |                DP paragraphname displays storage at the paragraph.     |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|_____|________________________________________________________________________|

|     | keys.                                                                  |

|     |     appears, type S TSO and press enter.                               |

./ ADD NAME=EXCHANGE 0101-98247-98247-1650-00057-00057-00000-BC0THOR
_______________________________________________________________________________
|     |09/04/1998             EXCHANGE                                 EXCHANGE|
|     |                                                                        |
|     |This program exchanges (interchanges two datasets on the same volume so |
|     |that the first DSNAME will point to the second dataset and the second   |
|     |DSNAME will point to the first dataset. Both datasets must already      |
|     |exist in the VTOC of the volume, and neither can be VSAM. This program  |
|     |does not make use of standard catalog and device allocation or serial-  |
|     |ization and so can be used to rename datasets even when they are in use |
|     |by other jobs. To minimize risk, the datasets are interchanged by       |
|     |rewriting the format 1 DSCB's for the two datasets so that the data     |
|     |records are interchanged while leaving the count and key portions       |
|     |as-is. In this way, modifications to the VTICIX are avoided, and no     |
|     |new records need to be created in the VTOC.                             |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |A VOLUME control card must precede the first EXCHANGE control card. It  |
|     |specifies the volume to be used for the EXCHANGEs that follow until     |
|     |another VOLUME control card is found. The VOLUME control card contains  |
|     |the word VOLUME in columns 1-6, blank in column 7, and has the volume   |
|     |serial in columns 8-13 left justified with trailing blanks.             |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |A two-card set is required for each pair of datasets to be interchanged.|
|     |The first contains the word EXCHANGE in columns 1-8, a blank in column  |
|     |9, the word DSN= in columns 10-13, and the full dataset name in columns |
|     |14-57 left justified with trailing spaces. The second card immediately  |
|     |follows the first and is blank in columns 1-9, has the word DSN= in     |
|     |columns 10-13, and the name of the second dataset in columns 14-57.     |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |A card having an asterisk in column 1 is treated as a comment, and is   |
|     |ignored by the program.                                                 |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |When any error is encountered, the program writes log records and       |
|     |terminates with a user abend. In this case, the log file may be very    |
|     |important, and should be studied in detail to determine whether any     |
|     |VTOC damage must be repaired. The VTOC repair can be done using         |
|     |IMASPZAP or CHRDUMP and the information in the log file.                |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |A log file is always written and contains all messages written to the   |
|     |SYSPRINT file as well as the content of all VTOC records read and       |
|     |written. The log file can be used to aid in VTOC recovery in case of a  |
|     |catastrophic error during processing, as it contains the VTOC details.  |
|     |Note that the VTOC records are given in hex, so the file must be viewed |
|     |in hex mode when using TSO EDIT or BROWSE.                              |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |Sample JCL is in BC0THOR.PDS.JCL(EXCHANGE)                              |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|_____|________________________________________________________________________|

./ ADD NAME=FTP      0102-98252-98275-1525-00057-00057-00000-BC0THOR
_______________________________________________________________________________
|     |10/02/1998             FILE TRANSFERS (PC <--> Mainframe)            FTP|
|     |                                                                        |
|     |1. If this transfer will be from the PC to the mainframe, be sure the   |
|     |   receiving mainframe PDS exists. Create it if necessary.              |
|     |2. Get out of SPF and to the TSO READY prompt.                          |
|     |3. Click on the File menu item from the Reflections menu. This will give|
|     |   a drop-down list.                                                    |
|     |4. On the drop-down, click on Transfer... to get to the Transfer Window.|
|     |5. Click the Setup... button and check on the IND$FILE tab to see that  |
|     |   the Host System is TSO and the Active Protocol is IND$FILE. If not,  |
|     |   click on the Setup menu item of the Reflection menu and set this up. |
|     |6. Set the Transfer Method to ASCII.                                    |
|     |7. Set If File Exists to Overwrite.                                     |
|     |8. Set Record Format to Fixed.                                          |
|     |9. Set the Drives window to the desired drive.                          |
|     |10. In the Local Directories window, double-click the desired directory.|
|     |11. In the Local File Names window, click the file to be transferred -  |
|     |    or if it is a new file, type the name.                              |
|     |12. In the TSO Host window on the right side middle, click on the       |
|     |    Show Host Files button. This will bring up a moving flashlight and  |
|     |    an hourglass while the mainframe is accessed to obtain a list of    |
|     |    your dataset. If this times out, you may be in ISPF and must get    |
|     |    out to a TSO READY prompt and start over.                           |
|     |13. Click on the desired mainframe directory to highlight it, then click|
|     |    and drag the PC file to it for a PC-to-Mainframe transfer. Or the   |
|     |    large arrow pointing to the right at the top of the window can be   |
|     |    clicked.                                                            |
|     |14. For a mainframe-to-pc transfer of a file shown in the directory     |
|     |    list, click on the file, then on the large left-pointing arrow at   |
|     |    the top of the window.                                              |
|     |15. For a mainframe-to-pc transfer of a member of a PDS, click the PDS  |
|     |    to highlight it, then type the member name in parentheses after the |
|     |    PDS name in the Name(Member/Password window at the top, then click  |
|     |    the large left-pointing arrow to begin transfer.                    |
|     |16. If a different high-level node is desired, try the Level button at  |
|     |    bottom of the window. My experience is that it times out before the |
|     |    directory is built, however. A possibility may be to type the fully |
|     |    qualified name in the Name(Member)/Password window.                 |
|     |                                                                        |

|     |09/04/1998               GTF                                         GTF|
|     |                                                                        |
|     |Allocate TEST.SYSx.TRACE with 10+ CYL, VBA,80,4096                      |
|     |     (STC has no security to write to USER02.* datasets)                |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |In SYSCON: S GTFDICK.RNT                                                |
|     |           R nn,TRACE=SVCP,JOBNAMEP                                     |
|     |           R nn,SVC=(13,19,20)            (decimal svc#s)               |
|     |           R nn,JOBNAME=jobname,END                                     |
|     |           R nn,U    (watch for GTF initialized message)                |
|     |To stop the GTF run, in SYSCON:                                         |

|     |                                                                        |

|     | 3. S GTFDICK.RNT                                                       |

|     |12/31/1998         IPCS (page 1)                                   IPCS1|
|     |                                                                        |
|     |WORKBENCH: 2.3.I                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |% before word in browse goes to address                                 |
|     |L before word in browse creates 24-bit PTR                              |
|     |H before word in browse creates 31-bit PTR                              |
|     |S in PTR column goes to address in entry                                |
|     |I in PTR column inserts a blank PTR                                     |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |W 10585E.             Where is 10585E? Dot saves time.                  |
|     |W 105000.+157C        Where is 10657C?                                  |
|     |CBF 6A9600 STRUC(TCB) Display TCB at 6A9600                             |
|     |LIST 6C.%             24-bit indirect                                   |
|     |LIST CVT+230?         31-bit indirect                                   |
|     |EQ CVT F3C0.          CVT means address F3C0                            |
|     |LIST 2C860. DIS LE(20) Display 20 bytes at address 2C860                |
|     |LIST 154C0.+2EC       Letting IPCS add                                  |
|     |LOCATE F4ECA0.        Locate F4ECA0                                     |
|     |F X'xx'    -or-   F C'ccc'  Find string                                 |
|     |  (Find always stops at breaks unless NOBREAK specified)                |
|     |L address. STR(ctl blk name)      gives displacements                   |
|     |L address. MOD(module name)       gives displacements                   |
|     |L address. ASID(x'hhhh')          Specific ASID memory                  |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |VERBX MTRACE          List WTO's in memory                              |
|     |VERBX TRACE 'ASID(5F)' Show trace entries for ASID 5F                   |
|     |ST REGS               PSW, Status, Regs                                 |
|     |VERBX LOGDATA         LOGREC in memory                                  |
|     |SUMMARY ANOMALY       Unusual Conditions                                |
|     |GTFTRACE SLIP USR SVC If GTF was running WITH slip TRACE                |
|     |VERBX SYMPTOMS        Symptom String                                    |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |To speed operations, use a print dataset to hold data,                  |
|     |then view with Edit/Browse in TSO Split-Screen                          |
|     |  Before IPCS initiated:                                                |
|     |     ATTR ATT1 RECFM(V B) LRECL(137)                                    |
|     |                 BLKSIZE(23476)                                         |
|     |     ALLOC F(IPCSPRNT) DA(IPCSPRNT)                                     |
|     |        UNIT(DISK) SPACE(5 1) CYLINDERS                                 |
|     |            USING(ATT1)                                                 |
|     |  SUMMARY FORMAT REGS PRINT NOTERM                                      |
|     |  CLOSE PRINT      <==== or BROWSE won't work !!!!!                     |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |SVCDUMPs: use ST FAILDATA                                               |
|     |SADMPs: use WORKSHEET REGS                                              |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |In BROWSE: IPCS Entry Panel to see REAL addresses:                      |
|     |        ADDRESS SPACE ==> ABSOLUTE                                      |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |LCCAPSW and LCCAPGR1 have PSW and Regs for last pgm check               |
|     |LCCAP2C1 has Control Reg1: pointer to Segment Table                     |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |

|     |    so rename it to another name ending in 'CMDS' such as MYCMDS.       |
|     |    Example: Rename ISPPROF(USERCMDS) ISPPROF(MYCMDS)                   |
|     | 2) Table to be updated must be in the ISPTABL file which is normally   |
|     |    in the dataset BC0THOR.ISPPROF.                                     |
|     | 3) On the Command Table Utility Menu enter the table prefix to be      |
|     |    used in the Application choice. CMDS will be postfixed to this.     |
|     | 4) To Edit a command, enter an "E" to its left, make the desired       |
|     |    changes, then move the cursor to "update" at the bottom and enter.  |
|     | 5) To use a modified table, rename it back to its original name        |
|     |    and get out of ISPF notmally, then get back into ISPF.              |
|     | 6) To install a USERCMDS table, build one using an application name    |
|     |    such as "MY". This creates member ISPPROF(MYCMDS). After finishing  |
|     |    and saving, get out of 3.9 and rename ISPPROF(MYCMDS) to            |
|     |    ISPPROF(USERCMDS) and get out of ISPF, then back in. The USER       |
|     |    application will be set up when the USERCMDS member is seen in      |
|     |    the ISPPROF dataset on ISPF initialization.                         |
|     |                                                                        |
|     | See Technical Support May 1989, Enterprise Systems                     |
|     | Journal July 1992, and SC34-4266 ISPF Dialog Management                |
|     | Guide and Reference: Appendix A.)                                      |
|     |                                                                        |
|     | To make changes in the ISPF Edit environment, get into edit            |
|     | .Click on the Menu item on the menu bar then press Enter.              |
|     |  .Type 1 for Settings and press Enter                                  |
|     |   .To move command line to top remove / on COMMAND LINE AT BOTTOM      |
|     |   .To have cursor home to command line remove / on TAB TO ACTION BAR   |
|     |   .To turn off underscores on input command lines click on the Colors  |
|     |    menu item on the menu bar and press enter.                          |
|     |    .Type 2 for CUA Attributes and press Enter                          |
|     |     .In the Highlight column replace all USCORE with NONE. Page down   |
|     |      to find them all.                                                 |
|     | .PF3 out to save changes                                               |
|     |                                                                        |
|     | To show panel name on screens: PANELID ON                              |
|     | To show PF key assignments: PFSHOW ON                                  |
|     |                                                                        |
|     | Add 'TEST' after ispf invocation command to turn off ESTAE so that     |
|     | normal abends occur without trapping.                                  |
|     |                                                                        |
|     | Chapter 11 of the IBM manual "ISPF EDIT and EDIT MACROS" contains a    |
|     | list of all the ISREDIT commands.                                      |
|     |                                                                        |
|     | Edit macros MUST be invoked from the command line in an ISPF EDIT      |
|     | session. They will NOT work properly if preceded by TSO, or if brought |
|     | in via the =3.9 command facility.                                      |
|     |                                                                        |
|     | Use the File pulldown with Setup selection to change the command line  |
|     | from TOP to BOTTOM of screen (and vice-versa).                         |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |

./ ADD NAME=LNKLST   0103-98251-00229-0758-00057-00068-00000-BC0THOR
_______________________________________________________________________________
|     |08/16/2000          LNKLST                                        LNKLST|
|     |                                                                        |
|     |To update a LINKLIST library:                                           |
|     | .Set up USER02.PDS.DATA(CSVLLART)                                      |
|     | .Issue O/S command F LLA,UPDATE=RT                                     |
|     | .Look for message CSV210I LIBRARY LOOKA...                             |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |Member CSVLLART in SYS1.PARMLIB contains:                               |
|     |         PARMLIB(USER02.PDS.DATA) SUFFIX(RT)                            |
|     |                                                                        |
|     | Use RESOLVE LL to list and/or change the LNKLST                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |Datasets in LNKLST *MUST* be cataloged in                               |
|     |the master catalog. (SPP not in master)                                 |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |Each system has its own master catalog. Be                              |
|     |sure to separately catalog in each system.                              |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |Console commands to add library SYS1.new.library to LNKLST on-the-fly:  |
|     |                                                                        |
|     | SETPROG LNKLST,DEFINE NAME=LNKLST05,COPYFROM=LNKLST00                  |
|     | SETPROG LNKLST,ACTIVATE NAME=LNKLST05                                  |
|     | SETPROG LNKLST,UPDATE JOB=*                                            |
|     | SETPROG LNKLST,ADD NAME=LNKLST00,DSNAME=SYS1.new.library               |
|     | SETPROG LNKLST,ACTIVATE NAME=LNKLST00                                  |
|     | SETPROG LNKLST,UPDATE JOB=*                                            |
|     | SETPROG LNKLST,UNDEFINE NAME=LNKLST05                                  |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |Note, attempt to activate may fail if any library in the list has become|
|     | unavailable. To correct, issue a DELETE command (change the ADD to     |
|     | DELETE in the 4th command).                                            |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |

|_____|________________________________________________________________________|
./ ADD NAME=LNKLST2  0101-02015-02016-0733-00057-00057-00000-BC0THOR
_______________________________________________________________________________
|     |01/16/2002             LNKLST (Continued)                       LNKLST2 |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |To make changes to the LNKLST on-the-fly:                               |
|     |1. Enter LOCMOD membername for some member in the dataset(s) to be      |
|     |   modified to be sure it is found in the LNKLST.                       |
|     |2. In SDSF LOG, enter /D PROG,LNKLST, whose display shows the name of   |
|     |   the current LNKLST SET. A listing similar to the below is shown:     |
|     |        CSV470I  16.43.04 LNKLST DISPLAY 697                            |
|     |        LNKLST SET LNKLST00 LNKAUTH=LNKLST                              |
|     |        ENTRY  APF  VOLUME   DSNAME                                     |
|     |          1     A   SYSTST   SYS1.LINKLIB                               |
|     |          2         SYSTS2   SYS1.XROLB                                 |
|     |  The name of the LNKLST SET is LNKLST00 as shown in the 2nd line above.|
|     |3. Note the name of the LNKLST SET, which will be used in the COPYFROM()|
|     |   parameter of the SETPROG,DEFINE command below.                       |
|     |4. Enter /SETPROG LNKLST,DEFINE,NAME(NEWLLSET),COPYFROM(currlnklstset)  |
|     |   which creates a new LNKLST SET identical to the one currently in     |
|     |   use on the system.                                                   |
|     |5. Enter /SETPROG LNKLST,DELETE,NAME(NEWLLSET),DSNAME(dsn-to-be removed)|
|     |   which will remove the named dataset from the NEWLLST list. Additional|
|     |   DELETE commands can be issued at this time, if desired.              |
|     |6. Enter /SETPROG LNKLST,ACTIVATE,NAME(NEWLLSET) which will activate    |
|     |   this new LNKLST SET, but does not affect any system jobs already     |
|     |   running that use the original LNKLST SET.                            |
|     |7. Enter /SETPROG LNKLST,UPDATE,JOB(*) which will result in all current |
|     |   jobs in execution being switched to the newly activated LNKLST SET,  |
|     |   freeing the original one.                                            |
|     |8. Enter /D PROG,LNKLST and check to be sure the active LNKLST SET is   |
|     |   now NEWLLSET.                                                        |
|     |9. You may want to verify that some member in the the dataset(s) removed|
|     |   is no longer available from the LNKLST by using the LOCMOD command.  |
|     |10. Enter /SETPROG LNKLST,UNDEFINE,NAME(original-lnklst-set-name) to    |
|     |   remove the definition of the original lnklst set.                    |
|     |11. Build a 'SYS1.PARMLIB(CSVLLAxx) member that contains a REMOVE state-|
|     |   ment for the dataset(s) that were removed from the new LNKLST SET    |
|     |   so they will be freed for renaming, deleting, editing, or whatever   |
|     |   needs to be done to them. The last two characters of the member      |
|     |   name (xx) are used in the modify command:                            |
|     |      /F LLA,UPDATE=xx                                                  |
|     |12. The modify command will free the dataset(s) from LLA control so that|
|     |   they can be manipulated.                                             |
|     |13. Perform any desired operations against the libraries now, such as   |
|     |   renaming, compressing, recreating, copying into, etc.                |
|     |14. If the original LNKLST SET in 'SYS1.PARMLIB(LNKLST00)' is now ok to |
|     |   be used, activate it by entering /T PROG=00 which will use that      |
|     |   member to rebuild the LNKLST and activate it.                        |
|     |15. Enter /SETPROG LNKLST,UPDATE,JOB(*) to switch all executing jobs    |
|     |   to this LNKLST SET.                                                  |
|     |16. Enter /SETPROG LNKLST,UNDEFINE,NAME(NEWLLSET)  to remove the        |
|     |   definition of NEWLLSET from the system.                              |
|     |17. Enter /D PROG.LNKLST and check to see that the LNKLST SET name is   |
|     |   correct.                                                             |
|     |18. Use the LOCMOD command to insure a member of the original dataset   |
|     |   is again available via the LNKLST.                                   |
|     |                                                                        |

|     |                                                                        |
|     |Daily job listing is in SAR database R under                            |
|     |job RUX2016U for software                                               |
|     |job R990006U for hardware                                               |
|     |job R990005U saves SYS1.LOGREC to SPP.R990005.LOGREC.DATA(+1) (2 gen)   |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |BC0THOR.PDS.JCL(IFCDIP00) has JCL to initialize a LOGREC dataset.       |
|     |BC0THOR.PDS.JCL(LOGRECSF) is a software report job from SYS1.LOGREC.    |
|     |BC0THOR.PDS.JCL(LOGRECHW) is a hardware report from SYS1.LOGREC.        |

|     |CUA=(06XX) :select any channel 06 device                                |
|     |CUA=(0603-0698) : select only devices 0603 through 0698                 |
|     |CUA=(0603,07B9,01F4) :select only devices specified (up to 8)           |

|     |TIME=(hhmm-hhmm) :time selection range                                  |
|     |DEV=(ESIO) :selects devices on ESCON links                              |
|     |DEV=(3390,3480) :selects all 3390 and 3480 devices (up to 8).           |
|     |DEV=(33XX,34XX) :selects all devices whose types begin 33 or 34         |
|     |DEV=(N27XX,N10XX) :excludes all devices whose types begin 27 or 10      |
|     |DEV=(N27XX,34XX) :invalid, can't mix excludes and includes.             |
|     |ERRORID=(nnnnn) :selects records for the given decimal error id         |
|     |PRINT=AL   :print all detail reports                                    |
|     |PRINT=DR   :print data reduction reports                                |
|     |PRINT=PS   :print detail edit and detail summary reports                |

|     |     A2 B2                                                              |
|     |     A3 B2                                                              |

|     |     A2 B3       (enter changes)                                        |

|     |     A1 B1                                                              |
|     |     A2 B1                                                              |

|     |The MAGSTAR is a robot tape device similar to the Storage Technology    |

|     |                                                                        |
|     |.DU 6000,8   Displays unit status (MIM)                                 |
|     |.DG 6000,8   Displays Global unit status (MIM)                          |

|     |                                                                        |
|     |OAM is the name of the started task used to manage the MAGSTAR. Look for|
|     |messages in the running log using SDSF. The OAM task is also referred to|
|     |as "LIB01" by some people.                                              |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |At times the MAGSTAR neds to be reset in order to be accessable by MVS. |
|     |Symptoms of this might be:                                              |
|     |MIM2120 DFHSM DFHSM UNABLE TO ALLOCATE                                  |
|     |MIM2042 DFHSM DFHSM RESIN2 DEVICES OFFLINE 341                          |
|     |  ==> 6101                                                              |
|     |Then, after a V 6101,ONLINE command is issued, the following display:   |
|     |IEE763I NAME=modname CODE=msg-code                                      |
|     |IOS551I NO PATHS PHYSICALLY AVAILABLE                                   |
|     |The IBM System Messages manual shows operator response is to contact    |
|     |hardware support. In the case of the Magstar, Ray Davis, Scott Suprun,  |
|     |and other Command Center people know how to reset the machine.          |

|     |________________________________________________________________________|
|     |                   IOCDS                                                |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |At a 3090 Console:                                                      |
|     |  Press INDEX (or PF2 or B) key                                         |
|     |  At INDEX screen type 07                                               |
|     |  On IOCDS Management Screen type In (ENTER)                            |
|     |     to move the cursor to line n.                                      |
|     |  Type An (ENTER) to invoke action n.                                   |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |________________________________________________________________________|
|     |               IPL Using an Alternate Nucleus                           |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |IPL'ing with an alternate nucleus or IOCDS:                             |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |In OPRCTL panel:                                                        |
|     |  L2            (LOAD - PARM)                                           |
|     |     1st byte = last character of IEANUC0x                              |
|     |     bytes 2-3 = last 2 characters of IOCDS                             |
|     |                 (default = 100)                                        |
|     |                                                                        |

|     |                                                                        |

|     |updating it or use TMONMVS for an immediate but temporary change.       |
|     |Change on the fly with MVS command "Set PROG=00" or use TMONMVS to make |
|     | ADD/CHG/DEL changes temporarily until next IPL                         |

|     |               dataset to disk                                          |
|     |SPIN class     Send current to SYSOUT class                             |
|     |PRINT ON class dest Open Screen Log                                     |
|     |PRINT          Print current screen                                     |
|     |PRINT OFF      Close Screen Log                                         |
|     |MODEL #        Set 3270 model nbr 2,3,4,5                               |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |Notes: Default for lll is userid                                        |
|     |       jjjjj can be jobname or * for current                            |
|     |       Get dsid from DD or PDDB request                                 |
|     |       dsname will be prefixed with userid                              |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |DA     Display all executing jobs                                       |
|     |DT     Display TSO users                                                |
|     |DS     Display system tasks                                             |
|     |DQ     Display input queues                                             |
|     |DI c   Display jobs in input class c                                    |
|     |AI c   Display jobs available for class c                               |
|     |HI c   Display held jobs in class c                                     |
|     |DF     Display output queues                                            |
|     |DO c   Display jobs in output class c                                   |
|     |WO     Display jobs with writer name specifi                            |
|     |AO c   Display available output in class c                              |
|     |HO c   Display held output in class c                                   |
|     |NJ     Display NJE input and output queues                              |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |Note: default for class is all classes                                  |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |FIND 'string' Col(ss,ee) Find next occurrenc                            |
|     |FALL 'string' Col(ss,ee) Find all occurrence                            |
|     |N/P    Reposition to Next, Previous DSID                                |
|     |COL #  Reposition to column #                                           |
|     |@/MD # Reposition to record #                                           |
|     |+/D #  Reposition forward # records                                     |
|     |-/UP # Reposition backward # records                                    |
|     |T/TOP B/BOTTOM Go to top or bottom of file                              |
|     |PF/PB # Reposition # pages                                              |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |Note, string can be delimited with blanks,                              |
|     |      single or double quotes or slashes.                               |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |TGPS   Shows list of top 20 users of SPOOL                              |

./ ADD NAME=RMFMON3B 0101-98357-98357-1444-00057-00197-00000-BC0THOR
_______________________________________________________________________________|
|     |12/23/1998             RMF MONITOR III                          RMFMON3B|
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     | FREF and BREF: These commands cause the report to display the next     |
|     |                interval (FREF) or the previous interval (BREF) for the |
|     |                report being viewed. These commands are especially      |
|     |                useful in doing historical analysis of earlier problems.|
|     |                The interval time is that specified by the RANGE, which |
|     |                can be set by the ROPTIONS command. To reduce keystrokes|
|     |                it is a good idea to set up a PF key for each of these  |
|     |                commands (use the KEYS command).                        |
|     | ROPTIONS: This is normally entered while within a report, rather than  |
|     |           from the primary menu. If entered from the primary menu, you |
|     |           will be asked for a report name. The report options permit   |
|     |           setting the following (press PF3 when finished):             |
|     |            DATE and TIME: Use this to look back at an earlier time, up |
|     |                           to 24-48 hours ago, depending on stored data.|
|     |            RANGE: This is the interval between successive displays. The|
|     |                   minimum is 100 seconds. Use this with the FREF and   |
|     |                   BREF commands.                                       |
|     |            CLASS: Report on ALL jobs, or only on TSO or STC or BATCH.  |
|     |            GROUP: Limit the report to a particular domain or perform-  |
|     |                   ance group.                                          |
|     |            SUMMARY: Include summary lines for CLASS or not.            |
|     |            CRITERION: Specify the lowest delay percentage to be shown  |
|     |                       for the report display. This defaults to 0% so   |
|     |                       that everything is shown, whether delayed or not.|
|     |                       You may find it better to use 5, 10, or more.    |
|     |            JOBS: If you say YES, after you press ENTER, you get a full |
|     |                  screen showing the jobs in the system. You can use    |
|     |                  this to specify the job(s) to be included on the      |
|     |                  report if desired. Place an S to the left of a job    |
|     |                  to include it on the report, or an X to exclude it.   |
|     |                                                                        |
|     | GO: This puts you in automatic update mode, and the date/time will be  |
|     |     set to current time. After each interval of time specified by the  |
|     |     value of RANGE, an updated screen is displayed. When in this mode  |
|     |     your PF keys are not recognized, and you cannot enter commands. To |
|     |     get out of GO mode, press ATTENTION (twice if in Supersession).    |
|     |                                                                        |
|     | DSINDEX: This shows you how much data is available for reporting by    |
|     |          date and time.                                                |
|     |                                                                        |
|     | JOB jjjjjjjj: The JOB command followed by a jobname gives an RMF Job   |
|     |               Delays Display, explaining any delays for the job in     |
|     |               detail. This is very helpful when a job is "hung" or     |
|     |               running very slowly.                                     |
|     |                                                                        |
|     | Cursor sensitivity: While in reports, you can move the cursor to fields|
|     |                     on the screen and press enter. If an expanded      |
|     |                     display is available for the field, it will be     |
|     |                     shown. When PF3 is pressed, you will be returned to|
|     |                     the display you were on before. If a jobname is    |
|     |                     selected at the cursor, the RMF Job Delays screen  |
|     |                     is produced. Other fields result in other displays.|

|     | When in this, or any report, you can scroll forward and back using PF8 |
|     | and PF7, just as in TSO Edit. In addition, you can enter a FIND jjjjjjj|
|     | command on the COMMAND line to locate a particular job. The TOP        |
|     | command will return you to the beginning of the display.               |
|     |                                                                        |
|     | The CRITERION was set to 10 using the ROPTIONS command so that only    |
|     | those jobs delayed 10% or more are displayed.                          |
|     |                                                                        |
|     | When evaluating job performance, first notice the WFL column. This     |
|     | shows the percentage of resources the job wants versus what it gets.   |
|     | A 100 here indicates it is getting all it wants and can use. A 0 here  |
|     | indicates it is getting nothing. Jobs with low WFL values should be    |
|     | evaluated further. If a number of jobs having low WFL values show the  |
|     | same Primary Reason, this may indicate a system-wide bottleneck. In    |
|     | this case, cursor to the name in the Primary Reason column and press   |
|     | ENTER for additional information.                                      |
|     |                                                                        |

|     | and press ENTER to see the RMF JOBS DISPLAY report which includes any  |
|     | details concerning its delays.                                         |

|     | When analyzing an earlier time, use the ROPTIONS command to set the    |
|     | date and time, them "walk" forward and back in time using the PF keys  |
|     | you have set up for FREF and BREF. This can provide a graphic picture  |
|     | of the changing environment that often helps understand why a problem  |
|     | occurred. This capability can be used with any of the reports, of      |
|     | course.                                                                |

|     |   MATCHLIM=1,ID=cccc,END                                               |

|     |                                                                        |

|     |                                                                        |
|     |SLIP SET,IF,LPAMOD=(IGC0005A,3178,3192),                                |
|     |   TRDATA=(STD,REGS,12R?,+200),A=TRACE,                                 |
|     |   ID=cccc,END                                                          |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |View in IPCS Command Screen using GTF SLIP                              |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |See SC28-1878 TSO/E System Programming Command Reference                |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |SVCDUMP after SLIP trap:                                                |
|     |  CVTSDBF => "type" "CPU", +10 => "REGS"                                |
|     |  followed by registers, then "PSW" and PSW content                     |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |PSA for particular processor:                                           |
|     |  CVTPCCAT points to a table of PCCA addr's                             |
|     |  (PR0, PR1, PR2, etc.). Each address+10                                |
|     |  contains CPU# (halfword), +18 = @ PSA                                 |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |SVCDUMP after SLIP SA Trap: in SUMDUMP, find                            |
|     |SLIP REGS SA                                                            |
|     |   PSW --> 1st 2 words                                                  |
|     |   ASIDS --> words 3,4                                                  |
|     |   REGS 0-15 --> words 5-20                                             |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |Abbreviations: Disable, ENable, ERrtyp, Jobname, JSpgm,                 |
|     |  Lpamod, MatchLim, Mode, Nucmod, PrcntLim, Pvtmod, RAnge,              |
