./ ADD NAME=SMF      0102-98251-02016-0918-00057-00057-00000-BC0THOR
_______________________________________________________________________________
|     |01/16/2002             SMF                                           SMF|
|     |                                                                        |
|     |Datasets may fill quickly due to DB2TRACE (types 100-102)               |
|     |records and NETSPY/NETVIEW (types 37, 39, and 150), and                 |
|     |due to CICS types. Also BLOCKADE uses type 213                          |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |View SMFDUMP output in J database of SAR for statistics on              |
|     |last run completed, which gives statistics by record type.              |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |Define SMF Dataset (SMF manual) PDS.JCL(SMFDEFIN)                       |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |Make SYS1.PARMLIB(SMFPRMzz) defining all SMF Datasets,                  |
|     |then issue SET SMF=zz. Will format the new dataset.                     |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |D SMF shows SMF and SMF Dataset status.                                 |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |I SMF forces SMF to switch datasets.                                    |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |SMF constantly writes records to the SYS1.MANX and SYS1.MANY datasets.  |
|     |When the current dataset fills, recording automatically switches, and   |
|     |the SMFDUMP job in SYS1.PROCLIB is scheduled to copy the full dataset   |
|     |to a GDG named SMF.DKIn001.SMFDATA(+!). After midnight, job DKIn001A    |
|     |is run, which forces an SMF dataset switch, and writes the final        |
|     |generation of the SMF.DKIn001A.SMFDATA for the day. Later, DKIn002A     |
|     |runs to copy all the generations for the day to a disk resident dataset |
|     |named SMF.DKIn002.RAWDATA.                                              |
|     |When a program that writes SMF records loops, the datasets fill quickly |
|     |and SMFDUMP is scheduled frequently so that at midnight a large number  |
|     |of generations have been created for the day's SMF data. The problem    |
|     |becomes evident later, when job DKIn002A abends SB37 since the huge     |
|     |volume of data will not fit on available DASD. DKIn002A's failure       |
|     |holds up later xKI... jobs, and the O/S SMF routines continue to pump   |
|     |out records. To correct this, you must identify the job that is creating|
|     |the records and get it stopped. Next, DKI0002A must be run successfully |
|     |to write the previous day's SMF data to a tape dataset, rather than to  |
|     |DASD, and the GDG's involved must be properly handled.                  |
|     |1. To find the record type causing the problem, look at job SMFDUMP     |
|     |   in SAR (J) for the system where the problem is happening. Page down  |
|     |   to the Summary Activity Report and look for a record type that is    |
|     |   a large percentage of the total (usually 90+%). Identify this        |
|     |   record's creator and take steps to stop it.                          |
|     |2. In SAR (R) look at the most recent execution of job DKI0001A (SYSB)  |
|     |   or DKI9001A (SYSA) and note the generation number created for        |
|     |   SMF.DKIn001.SMFDATA.GnnnnV00. This is the last generation to be      |
|     |   included in the rerun of DKIn002A which archives yesterday's data.   |
|     |3. Any generations BEYOND this are for today's data, and must be        |
|     |   renamed to prevent their being picked up by the rerun od DKIn002A.   |
|     |   The TSO/ISPF Data Set List Utility (=3.4 in ISPF or 2.4.1.4 in WB)   |
|     |   can be used for this. A good method is to replace the final "0"      |
|     |   with an "X". That should leave a number of generations, with the     |
|     |   last being the one shown in the DKIn001A run.                        |
|     |   (Continued...)                                                       |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|_____|________________________________________________________________________|
./ ADD NAME=SMF2     0100-02016-02016-0934-00057-00057-00000-BC0THOR
_______________________________________________________________________________
|     |01/16/2002             SMF (Continued)                          SMF2    |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |4. The SMFDUMP proc in SYS1.PROCLIB needs to be modified so that it     |
|     |   cannot run and create any new generation until DKIn002A has been     |
|     |   successfully rerun. When finished, that job will have deleted all    |
|     |   generations of SMF.DKIn001.SMFDATA that it archived. Either "break"  |
|     |   the SMFDUMP PROC so it gets a JCL error when run, or change its      |
|     |   //DUMPOUT DD to use a different dataset name.                        |
|     |5. Call the Command Center and have them add an override to the end of  |
|     |   the DKIn002A job to write the data to a tape, rather than to disk.   |
|     |   The added DD should be:                                              |
|     |      //SORTOUT DD UNIT=3590-1,LABEL=(1,SL,,,RETPD=3)                   |
|     |6. Have the Command Center restart the DKIn002A job after the override  |
|     |   has been added.                                                      |
|     |7. When DKIn002A runs successfully, it will delete all its input        |
|     |   generations for SMF.DKIn001.SMFDATA. Use ISPF 3.4 (or WB 2.4.1.4)    |
|     |   to verify this.                                                      |
|     |8. Use ISPF 3.4 (or WB 2.4.1.4) to rename all the datasets renamed in   |
|     |   step 3 above back to their original names and verify that they are   |
|     |   now cataloged under the SMF.DKIn001.SMFDATA base.                    |
|     |9. If the SMFDUMP job ran during all this and created a new dataset,    |
|     |   it must now be renamed to follow the last generation of the          |
|     |   SMF.DKIn001.SMFDATA group.                                           |
|     |10. Put the SMFDUMP PROC in SYS1.PROCLIB back the way it was originally.|
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |

|     |                                                                        |

|     |                S MQBBPAS                                               |
|     |         STOP:  P MQBBISS                                               |
|     |                P MQBBPAS                                               |
|     |                P MQBBCAS                                               |
|     |                IF THEY WILL NOT STOP THEN CANCEL                       |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |CAACF2   START: THERE IS NO START COMMAND ISSUED FOR CA-ACF2 IN EITHER  |
|     |                MEMBER IEACMD00 OR MEMBER COMMND00 IN SYS1.PARMLIB.     |
|     |                ACF2 IS AUTOMATICALLY STARTED BECAUSE OF THE PRESENCE   |
|     |                OF THE "CAISEC00" MEMBER IN SYS1.PARMLIB  THIS MEMBER   |
|     |                CAUSES THE ACF2 STARTED TASK TO BE STARTED WITH THE     |
|     |                PARAMETERS IN MEMBER "CAIACF01".  THE "CAIACF01" MEMBER |
|     |                MEMBER INSTRUCTS ACF2 TO USE A DEFAULT SYSTEM ID OF     |
|     |                "SYSB".  IT ALSO ENSURES THAT THE ACF2 AUTOMATIC BACK-  |
|     |                UP FUNCTION WILL EXECUTE AT THE DEFINED TIME OF 23:30.  |
|     |                NOTE:  IF IT IS NECESSARY TO START CA-ACF2 MANUALLY AT  |
|     |                ANY TIME, THE FOLLOWING COMMAND MUST BE USED:           |
|     |                S ACF2,PARM='SYSID(SYSB)'                               |
|     |                YOU MAY GET ALLOCATION RECOVERY MESSAGES FOR ACF2       |
|     |                COMPLAINING THAT DATASET IMS.IMT.ACFT61.ACFLOAD CANNOT  |
|     |                BE FOUND. IF SO, REPLY CANCEL AND ACF2 WILL CONTINUE    |
|     |                INITIALIZATION NORMALLY.                                |
|     |         STOP:  P ACF2 - ONLY AFTER ALL RUNNING JOBS, STARTED TASKS,    |
|     |                         AND JES2 HAVE FINISHED EXECUTING.              |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |CAIENF   START: S CAIENF FIRST BE SURE CAS9KEYS AND CAS9 HAVE EXECUTED  |
|     |                (SEE CA90S). THIS TASK MUST BE EXECUTING BEFORE ANY     |
|     |                CICS REGION IS STARTED.                                 |
|     |         STOP:  P ENF (AFTER ALL OF THE FOLLOWING MESSAGES DISPLAY:)    |
|     |                CAS9225A - VERIFY CA-ENF SHUTDOWN REQUEST               |
|     |                CAS9226A - WARNING: APPLICATIONS WHICH USE CA-ENF ...   |
|     |                CAS9227A - REPLY "Y" TO THE REPLY ID FOR MESSAGE        |
|     |                           CAS9227A TO CONTINUE TERMINATION.            |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |CAJCLCHK START: NOTHING. FIRST BE SURE CAS9KEYS AND CAS9 HAVE EXECUTED  |
|     |                (SEE CA90S).                                            |
|     |         STOP:  NOTHING TO STOP, JUST PROCEED WITH MVS SHUTDOWN.        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |CAVIEW:  SEE SAR                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |

|     |09/08/1998        SYNCSORT                                      SYNCSORT|
|     |                                                                        |
|     |To throw out duplicate records:                                         |
|     |      SUM FIELDS=NONE                                                   |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |PARM=(VLTEST=1) permits records in variable                             |
|     |  files shorter than where sort key is                                  |
|     |  located. Key is treated as low-values for                             |
|     |  these records.                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |INCLUDE COND=(pp,ll,ff,cc,vvv,xxx,....)                                 |
|     |OMIT COND=(pp,ll,ff,cc,vvv,xxx,...)                                     |
|     | Where:                                                                 |
|     |   pp = begin column                                                    |
|     |   ll = length of field (and vvv)                                       |
|     |   ff = data type                                                       |
|     |   cc = condition: EQ, NE, GT, GE, LT, LE                               |
|     |   vvv = comparison value as:                                           |
|     |         C'ccc'                                                         |
|     |         X'xxxx'                                                        |
|     |         +nnn                                                           |
|     |         -nnn                                                           |
|     |         nnnn                                                           |
|     |         pp,ll,ff                                                       |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |

./ ADD NAME=TMONMVS1 0102-98357-99242-1342-00057-00057-00000-BC0THOR
_______________________________________________________________________________|
|     |08/30/1999             TMONMVS Page 1                           TMONMVS1|
|     |                                                                        |
|     |            USING TMONMVS to DISPLAY DASD I/O DATA                      |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |  TMONMVS can be used to obtain information on the busiest DASD         |
|     |  devices, and which datasets are being used on a volume, and           |
|     |  the jobs using these datasets. Following is a procedure for           |
|     |  doing this.                                                           |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |  1. At the TMONMVS PRIMARY MENU on the SELECTION line, type            |
|     |     =1.6 and press ENTER. This will bring up the                       |
|     |     I/O CONFIGURATION MONITOR screen.                                  |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |  2. Press PF5 to get the DASD ACTIVITY MONITOR screen.                 |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |  3. Tab to the % DEV BUSY _ field and press ENTER. This will           |
|     |     sort the display in descending order by % DEV BUSY. The            |
|     |     first device shown will be the busiest. Pressing ENTER             |
|     |     will update the display. (To get back to the                       |
|     |     I/O CONFIGURATION MONITOR screen, press PF3).                      |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |  4. Decide which DASD volume is to be analyzed and move the            |
|     |     cursor to its DEV NUM, then press ENTER. This will invoke          |
|     |     the DEVICE DETAIL SELECTION MENU. On the SELECTION line,           |
|     |     type the number 2 and press ENTER. A message will appear           |
|     |     saying I/O PROFILE SUCCESSFULLY STARTED.                           |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |  5. On the SELECTION line, enter =5.1 and press ENTER. You             |
|     |     will then see a PROFILE STATUS/SELECTION menu, and the top         |
|     |     line should show the request you just made, with PENDING           |
|     |     in the STATUS COLUMN. This means TMONMVS is monitoring the         |
|     |     DASD volume, which takes a little time. Every few seconds,         |
|     |     press ENTER, until the STATUS changes to COMPLETE.                 |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |  6. Move the cursor to the SEG field at the left side of the           |
|     |     COMPLETE report line and press ENTER. This will bring up           |
|     |     the DASD I/O PROFILE screen.                                       |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |  7. Press PF6 to get the DASD DATA SET I/O ACTIVITY PROFILE            |
|     |     screen. This shows the datasets being used on the volume,          |
|     |     and the jobs using them. This can be very helpful in               |
|     |     analyzing DASD I/O problems.                                       |
|     |                                                                        |
|     | To activate a system console, type CONS on the command line,           |
|     | giving a list of consoles. For SYSA choose 01. For SYSB scroll         |
|     | down and choose 74.                                                    |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |

./ ADD NAME=TRACEBR  0100-98357-98357-1450-00057-00057-00000-BC0THOR
_______________________________________________________________________________|
|     |12/23/1998             TRACING WILD BRANCHES                    TRACEBR |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                 Tracing Wild Branches Using SLIP and GTF               |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |  1. Build an SBT SLIP trap to trace all branches to a                  |
|     |     particular location. An example, which would show all              |
|     |     branches to offset +AC in a module named DXT0230U in the           |
|     |     private area running under the jobname RUX1077W and                |
|     |     writing trace records containing standard data (STD) and           |
|     |     registers (REGS) would be:                                         |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |          SLIP SET,SBT,A=TRACE,TRDATA=(STD,REGS),J=RUX1077W,            |
|     |               PVTMOD=(DXT0230U,AC,AC),ID=RNT1,END                      |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |  2. If a dump is desired in addition, use A+TRDUMP and add the         |
|     |     dump condition (such as C=0C4). A range of offsets may be          |
|     |     traced. To trace all references between +86 and +148, use          |
|     |     PVTMOD=(DXT0230U,86,148).                                          |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |  3. When the SLIP trap is entered, a message will indicate it          |
|     |     is active, but that GTF is not active.                             |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |  4. Start GTF and specify:                                             |
|     |          TRACE=SLIP,JOBNAMEP                                           |
|     |          JOBNAME=RUX1077W                                              |
|     |          END                                                           |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |  5. On completion, stop the GTF run (and the SLIP trap, if             |
|     |     necessary). The SLIP trap will notify you the first time           |
|     |     there is a hit, but not after that.                                |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |  6. Using IPCS, point to the GTF trace dataset and on the              |
|     |     COMMAND screen (4) enter GTF. Say yes when asked if the            |
|     |     dataset contains only trace data.                                  |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |  7. The standard SLIP trace records (S+U) contain the branch           |
|     |     information as follows:                                            |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |        IADR: The address of the branch instruction to                  |
|     |              DXT0230U+AC                                               |
|     |        INS:  The branch instruction itself, in hex.                    |
|     |        OPSW: The PSW, as updated by the branch instruction.            |
|     |              The PSW address should therefore be the address           |
|     |              of the instruction being traced.                          |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|_____|________________________________________________________________________|
./ ADD NAME=TRANSMIT 0101-99088-99242-1351-00057-00057-00000-BC0THOR
_______________________________________________________________________________
|     |08/30/1999           TSO TRANSMIT(XMIT) COMMAND                 TRANSMIT|
|     |                                                                        |
|     |The TRANSMIT command can be used to unload a PDS to a flat file which   |
|     |can then be sent to the the PC hard drive using Reflection/IND$FILE.    |
|     |The TSO RECEIVE command can be used to rebuild the PDS from this flat   |
|     |file. This makes it possible to send load modules to another mainframe  |
|     |site.                                                                   |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |Simply copying a load module will not work, as the directory entry at   |
|     |receiving site contains none of the information needed by Program Fetch.|
|     |An IEBCOPY unload cannot be used with Reflections, either, since this   |
|     |creates a RECFM=VS flat file that Reflections/IND$FILE cannot handle.   |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |The XMIT command requires, as its first parameter, an address that is   |
|     |given as nodename.userid. To find the nodename, get in SDSF and use     |
|     |the NODE command. In the list, look for OWNNODE in the status column,   |
|     |and use the value in the nodename column for that row. Nodename BCV was |
|     |valid when this was written. An example TRANSMIT command to unload a PDS|
|     |named TEST.LOADLIB to a flat file called BC0THOR.UNLOAD would be:       |
|     |XMIT BCV.BC0THOR DSNAME('TEST.LOADLIB') PDS OUTDSNAME('BC0THOR.UNLOAD') |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |Output from the XMIT command is DSORG=PS,RECFM=FB,LRECL=80,BLKSIZE=3120 |
|     |which is acceptable to Reflection/IND$FILE. To transfer this flat file  |
|     |from the mainframe to the PC using Reflection/IND$FILE, first get to a  |
|     |TSO READY prompt outside of ISPF, then select the SETUP menu item in    |
|     |Reflection and set Active Protocol: IND$FILE, Host System: TSO, Max     |
|     |size: Disabled, then choose Advanced. Enter blanks in Logical Record    |
|     |Length and Block Size and uncheck both boxes under CR/LF processing.    |
|     |Set Space allocation units to default. Enter OK until back to the       |
|     |Reflection screen, then choose File from the menu and Transfer from the |
|     |drop-down list. In the Local file names window (top left) type the name |
|     |of the PC file to be created (for example, C:\UNLD) and in the TSO Host |
|     |Name(member) window (top right) type the name of the mainframe file you |
|     |created using the XMIT command. Enter the fully qualified name enclosed |
|     |in apostrophes (for example: 'BC0THOR.UNLOAD') and in the center of     |
|     |the screen set Transfer Method: Binary, IF File Exists: overwrite, and  |
|     |Record Format: fixed. Finally, select the top center transfer box with  |
|     |arrows pointing left to initiate the transfer.                          |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |Once the PC file is created, you can attach it to an email to send it   |
|     |to the receiving mainframe site. At the other end, the attached file    |
|     |must be saved to the PC hard drive, then transferred to their mainframe |
|     |using the same Reflection/IND$FILE settings above. Finally, they must   |
|     |use the TSO RECEIVE command to recreate the load library. First issue   |
|     |the TSO command: PROFILE PROMPT, since this must be in effect for the   |
|     |RECEIVE command to work. A sample RECEIVE command to restore the flat   |
|     |file BC0THOR.RCVD is:                                                   |
|     |     RECEIVE INDSNAME('BC0THOR.RCVD')                                   |
|     |If successful, you are asked to reply with parameters, which means you  |
|     |enter the dsname to be used for the reload. This PDS will be created    |
|     |if it does not exist. To restore the file with name BC0THOR.RELOADED,   |
|     |you would enter:                                                        |
|     |     DSNAME('BC0THOR.RELOADED')                                         |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|_____|________________________________________________________________________|
./ ADD NAME=TRANSMT2 0100-00229-00229-1624-00057-00057-00000-BC0THOR

|     |08/16/2000            TSO TRANSMIT (XMIT) COMMAND continued     TRANSMT2|
|     |                                                                        |
|     |1. Create a PDS containing only the load module to be sent.             |
|     |2. XMIT INDSNAME(dsname.from.step1) PDS OUTDSNAME(sent.file.name)       |
|     |3. To test the result:                                                  |
|     |       PROFILE PROMPT                                                   |
|     |       RECEIVE INDSNAME(sent.file.name)                                 |
|     |       Reply: DSNAME(receive.file.name)                                 |
|     |       Use TSO TEST command to verify contents                          |
|     |4. EMAIL sent.file.name to recipient                                    |
|     |5. Recipient transfers sent.file.name to his mainframe                  |
|     |6. Recipient enters commands in step 3 above to obtain the data.        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |

|     |01/15/2002         VARY COMMANDS                                    VARY|
|     |                                                                        |
|     |Network terminal off: V NET,INACT,ID=L22TRM01                           |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |Printer 71 in Roanoke on the converter was taken off for                |
|     |maintenance. On return, could not get it back online.                   |
|     |Finally, $S PRT71 followed by V A0F,ONLINE resulted in                  |
|     |intervention required and it came back. Earlier VARYs                   |
|     |(online and offline) gave messages saying the last path                 |
|     |to the device was being removed.                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |Printer 71 in Roanoke on CHPID 8A was accidentally dis-                 |
|     |connected during operation by C&P leaving software with                 |
|     |a job in progress. Various VARYs, etc, did not help.                    |
|     |Neither did attempts to CONFIG the CHPID on/offline. The                |
|     |printer was IML'ed at Roanoke with no help. As a last                   |
|     |reset the channel extender, then IMLed the printer. After               |
|     |that, the Command Center was able to VARY the path and                  |
|     |unit online and resume operation.                                       |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |Move external tape drive 670 to the Y2K LPAR:                           |
|     |  1) At a SYSB MVS console:                                             |
|     |       . V,670,OFFLINE,GLOBAL                                           |
|     |       DS P,670,1               (shows 9B and 1B)                       |
|     |       V PATH(670-67F,1B),OFFLINE                                       |
|     |       CF CHP(1B),OFFLINE                                               |
|     |  2) At a Y2K LPAR MVS console:                                         |
|     |       CF CHP(1B),ONLINE                                                |
|     |       V PATH(670,1B),ONLINE                                            |
|     |       V 670,ONLINE                                                     |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |When running SMPE you get message: AT LEAST ONE OFFLINE UNIT(S) NEEDED..|
|     |   FOR RECEIVE SMPCSI                                                   |
|     |   FOR VOLUME SMPE04                                                    |
|     |   OFFLINE                                                              |
|     |   1899 ........                                                        |
|     |  *09 IEF238D BC0THORD REPLY DEVICE NAME OR CANCEL                      |
|     |Procedure to fix this:                                                  |
|     | 1. On SYSA or SYSB (wherever SMPE04 can be seen) use TMONMVS to get the|
|     |    device id:                                                          |
|     |    A. Issue command DEVUSER.                                           |
|     |    B. Tab to the VOLSER field and type SMPE04, then (enter).           |
|     |    C. The UNIT field should now contain a 4-digit (hex) unit number.   |
|     | 2. On the same system, use SYSCON or SDSF to enter the command         |
|     |    D M=DEV(xxxx) where xxxx is the unit number from step 1.C. In the   |
|     |    resulting display, choose any CHP that has Y's under it. This will  |
|     |    be a 2-digit (hex) number.                                          |
|     | 3. On the original system with the outstanding reply, use SYSCON or    |
|     |    SDSF to enter the commands (omit the M/ prefix in SYSCON):          |
|     |        M/CF CHP(xx),ONLINE        where xx is the CHP from step 2.     |
|     |        M/VARY xxxx,ONLINE         where xxxx is unit from step 1.C.    |
|     |        /R nn,xxxx                 where xxxx is unit from step 1.C.    |

|     |put in production.                                                      |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |The License Management is effected by a started task originally named   |
|     |LMSINIT, but renamed CLFINIT to avoid conflict here. S CLFINIT must be  |
|     |done before license info is available for testing, production. Insure   |
|     |the startup parms in SPP.COMPWARE.MLMS101.SLMSCNTL(LMINPARM) show UPDATE|
|     |so that any new/changed licenses will be recognized. (See CLFINIT PROC).|
|     |                                                                        |
|     |To see PTF's applied, get into a test session with source code showing  |
|     |on the screen, then enter the command: SHOW ZAP.                        |

|     |password is X59PfU (case-sensitive).                                    |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |System-wide XPEDITER defaults can be set using a CLIST to allocate the  |
|     |libraries and invoke XPEDITER and including the INSTALL parameter. For  |
|     |example, TSO XPED INSTALL in the case of V6R6M0. The CLIST is in        |
|     |SYS1.CLIST.                                                             |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |When compiling under the XPEDITER PREPARE option, include APOST, CSYN,  |
|     |and LANGLVL(2) for the IVP programs. Add SPP.XPEDTSO.V6R6M0.SAMPLIB to  |

|     |containing CBLTDLI to the SYSLIB and enter ENTRY DLITCBL in the SYSIN.  |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |When testing TRIMPP, add the library containing program ADSIM001 to the |
|     |LOADLIB panel: SPP.XPEDTSO.V6R6M0.LOADLIB.                              |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |IMS commands useful when testing the TRIMPP program/transaction:        |
|     |/DIS A     Shows active users. After setting up in XPEDITER/TSO, your   |
|     |           userid will show with class 31 if all went well.             |
|     |/DIS DB XPIMSDB Shows status of the XPIMSDB database. It should not be  |
|     |           stopped. If it is, use the STA command to start it.          |
|     |/DIS PGM ADSIM001 Shows status of the ADSIM001 program. Start it if it  |
|     |           is stopped.                                                  |
|     |/DIS TRAN XPEDTX1 Shows status of the XPEDTX1 transaction. Start it if  |
|     |           is stopped.                                                  |
|     |/END followed by /RCL terminates the IMS session when finished.         |
|     |/TEST MFS  Should precede the initiating command /FOR TRIMPP so that    |
|     |           the format is obtained from the test libraries.              |

|     |from Compuware using the CWLMA CLIST, then execute the CLFINIT CLIST    |

./ ADD NAME=XPEDSRT1 0102-99340-99343-1053-00057-00057-00000-BC0THOR
_______________________________________________________________________________
|     |12/09/1999         XPEDITER TESTING IN SORT EXITS               XPEDSRT1|
|     |                                                                        |
|     |When testing a sort exit using XPEDITER, the batch execution method is  |
|     |used, where JCL is submitted to batch via XPEDITER panel 4.1, and the   |
|     |test begins when the exit routine is entered.                           |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |1. Assemble the sort exit for XPEDITER so that a DDIO file is created.  |
|     |   Note the dsnames for the DDIO file and the load library, as they will|
|     |   be needed below.                                                     |
|     |2. Build the sort control statements to be used. They will be a modified|
|     |   version of normal sort control statements, but modified so that      |
|     |   XTASKLIB is specified for the library containing the exit to be      |
|     |   tested. For example: MODS E15=(MYEXIT,15000,XTASKLIB,N). Other       |
|     |   control statements require no changes.                               |
|     |3. Build the execution JCL, which will be a modified version of the     |
|     |   normal JCL:                                                          |
|     |   A. Change the EXEC statement so that it contains at least:           |
|     |      EXEC PGM=XPDSORT,PARM='CORE=MAX,NOSTAE,NOSTIMER,VSIO=NONE'        |
|     |   B. Add an XTASKLIB DD statement pointing to the load library that    |
|     |      contains the exit to be tested.                                   |
|     |   C. Modify the SYSIN DD statement to point to the modified control    |
|     |      statements created in step 2.                                     |
|     |4. Create an XPEDITER script member in a PDS having RECFM=FB,LRECL=80   |
|     |   that contains the following:                                         |
|     |      SET DYNAMIC xxxxxxxx                                              |
|     |      BEFORE xxxxxxxx.                                                  |
|     |      AFTER xxxxxxxx.                                                   |
|     |   In these statements, xxxxxxxx is the member name of the sort exit to |
|     |   be tested in the XTASKLIB file. Be sure to include the periods in the|
|     |   BEFORE and AFTER statements. If the exit routine's member name is not|
|     |   the same as its CSECT name, use an INTERCEPT statement rather than   |
|     |   the 3 statements above. An example is:                               |
|     |       INTercept sort-exit LOAdm load-mod-name                          |
|     |   Also, if any assembly module does VCON modifications, use a          |
|     |       SET EXCLUDE xxxxxxxx.                                            |
|     |   where xxxxxxxx is the module name.                                   |
|     |5. In a WORKBEMCH ISPF session, use =2.3.XP to enter XPEDITER panels,   |
|     |   choose option 3 - BATCH to get the PROCESS EXECUTE JCL screen and    |
|     |   type SE on the command line and press Enter to get the SETUP MENU.   |
|     |   Enter to get to the TEST SETUP MENU.                                 |
|     |   A. Choose 1 - LOADLIBS to get to the BASE PRODUCT DATASETS screen    |
|     |      and enter:                                                        |
|     |      (1) ===> 'SPP.XPEDTSO.TEST.LOADLIB'                               |
|     |      (2) ===> 'SYS1.LINKLIB'                                           |
|     |      (3) ===> 'library containing the exit to be tested'               |
|     |      Press Enter to return to the SETUP MENU.                          |
|     |   B. Choose 2 - DDIO to get to the DDIO FILES panel and enter the name |
|     |      of the DDIO file in (1).                                          |
|     |      Press Enter to return to the SETUP MENU.                          |
|     |   C. Choose 3 - INCLUDES to get the TEST SCRIPT LIBRARIES panel and    |
|     |      in (1) enter the name of the script library used in step 4.       |
|     |      Press Enter to return to the SETUP MENU.                          |
|     |   D. Press PF3 to get back to the PROCESS EXECUTE JCL screen where     |
|     |      you will enter the dsname and member name for the sort JCL that   |
|     |      was created in step 2 and press Enter to Enter.                   |
|_____|________________________________________________________________________|
./ ADD NAME=XPEDSRT2 0101-99343-99343-1110-00057-00057-00000-BC0THOR
_______________________________________________________________________________
|     |12/09/1999             XPEDITER Testing in SORT Exits           XPEDSRT2|
|     |                                                                        |
|     |  D. The SELECT JOB STEP should be displayed now.                       |
|     |     (1) Type RUN on the command line.                                  |
|     |     (2) Move the cursor to the red underscore at the left of the line  |
|     |         showing the step that will be tested. Type the letter I over   |
|     |         red underscore, then tab to the INITSCR column.                |
|     |     (3) Type the member name of the script created in step4 in the     |
|     |         INITSCR column.                                                |
|     |     (4) Press Enter to submit the job and begin the test. Several      |
|     |         informative messages will be given, such as: JOB IS EXECUTING, |
|     |         JOB IS NOT READY TO CONNECT, WAITING FOR CONNECTION TO VTAM,   |
|     |         etc. Wait until the XPEDITER SOURCE screen appears, then begin |
|     |         testing. If message NO DDIO DATASET FOUND FOR XPDSORT ...      |
|     |         appears, press PF12 and wait.                                  |
|     |7. To begin testing, press PF9 to begin single stepping through the code|
|     |   or set breakpoints at desired places and press PF12 to run to the    |
|     |   next breakpoint. The GPREGS command will cause regsiter contents     |
|     |   to be diaplayed. Peek, Display, DP, and Keep commands can be used to |
|     |   display and modify data. The V line command can be used to display   |
|     |   and modify instructions.                                             |
|     |8. If the test session is terminated while the sort is still active, try|
|     |   not to use the EXIT or QUIT commands, as they can cause a S0C4 abend |
|     |   and may reduce your region size thereafter. Instead, use the Primary |
|     |   Commands:                                                            |
|     |     MOVE 16 TO SORT-RETURN.                                            |
|     |     GO 1    (PF9)                                                      |
|     |     GOTO nnnnn (nnnn is the RELEASE or RETURN statement number)        |
|     |     GO 1    (PF9 repeatedly until at the statement following the sort.)|
|     |     GOBACK                                                             |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
|     |                                                                        |
